    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer6156560078645502739">Jojo Harvey is a dead ringer for Jessica Rabbit and the most ferocious literary agent in town. A former NYPD cop, she now lives in London making million-dollar book deals while trying to make partner at her firm . . . all the while sleeping with the boss man.<br/><br/>Lily Wright is an author who believes in karma, and is waiting for the sky to fall after stealing her former best fr</span>
  <span id="freeText6156560078645502739" style="display:none">Jojo Harvey is a dead ringer for Jessica Rabbit and the most ferocious literary agent in town. A former NYPD cop, she now lives in London making million-dollar book deals while trying to make partner at her firm . . . all the while sleeping with the boss man.<br /><br />Lily Wright is an author who believes in karma, and is waiting for the sky to fall after stealing her former best friend's man. Though her first book failed to sell, her life turns upside down when her most recent book becomes a huge bestseller.<br /><br />Gemma Hogan is an event designer extraordinaire, but her personal life is nonexistent after losing the love of her life and her best friend in one fell swoop. To make matters worse, her father has just left her mother. While taking care of her mother, she e-mails a close colleague about her frustrations, who in turn forwards the hilarious e-mails to a famous literary agent named Jojo Harvey, who just happens to represent her former friend, now enemy, Lily Wright. . . .<br /><br />Written in the charming and chatty voice that has become Marian Keyes's signature style, this hilarious and heartwarming novel proves there are three sides to every story . . . especially in the world of publishing!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89366799" />
    <a title="Tiffany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1545272-tiffany"><img alt="Tiffany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468630507p2/1545272.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89366799?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiffany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiffany" href="/user/show/1545272-tiffany">Tiffany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140295993" href="/book/show/924487.The_Other_Side_of_the_Story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1545272-tiffany?shelf=international-fiction">international-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1545272-tiffany?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1545272-tiffany?shelf=i-want-my-time-back">i-want-my-time-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1545272-tiffany?shelf=light-reads">light-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89366799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13633842585662722590">2.5<br/><br/>Mildly entertaining, but I HATED the characters. <br/><br/>1. Gemma. GET OVER IT. Yes, your best friend "stole" your boyfriend (not EVEN), but it happened THREE YEARS ago. And don't even get me started on Gemma's mother. What an IDIOT. I can understand being devastated after your husband of thirty-five years leaves you for a younger woman, but to make your idiot daughter take care of you for MONTHS as if you're terminally ill? GIVE ME A DAMN BREAK. <br/><br/>2. Jojo. I actually liked Jojo. I didn't have a proble</span>
  <span id="freeText13633842585662722590" style="display:none">2.5<br /><br />Mildly entertaining, but I HATED the characters. <br /><br />1. Gemma. GET OVER IT. Yes, your best friend "stole" your boyfriend (not EVEN), but it happened THREE YEARS ago. And don't even get me started on Gemma's mother. What an IDIOT. I can understand being devastated after your husband of thirty-five years leaves you for a younger woman, but to make your idiot daughter take care of you for MONTHS as if you're terminally ill? GIVE ME A DAMN BREAK. <br /><br />2. Jojo. I actually liked Jojo. I didn't have a problem with her affair with Mark, and I liked her ambition. Every time I reached a Jojo chapter, I breathed a small sigh of relief at having been done a ridiculous Gemma one.<br /><br />3. Lily. OK, she was kind of sweet. But what an idiot with money, and she was such a WIMP. Reading a Lily chapter was like watching a train wreck, and then it just got old. <br /><br />Marian Keyes, I will give you ONE MORE CHANCE, and then I'm calling it quits. Oh, and by the way, your novels DO NOT need to be this long. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13633842585662722590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17801570005552467993" style="display:none">I was not expecting this book to be that good. I found instead that i was addicted to the three main characters' stories. This book is a typical girly novel, where the main characters are obsessed with their relationships. <div id="review_34206567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34206567" />
    <a title="Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1579129-robyn"><img alt="Robyn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34206567?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robyn" href="/user/show/1579129-robyn">Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34206567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5633485707713897273">What a welcome respite from the heaviness I’ve seemed to be reading lately. This is a not-quite-chic-lit book, and the characters, what characters they are! This is my first experience with Marian Keyes, and I have to read more. This particular novel takes place in Ireland and London (as I suppose most of her work does), and I loved reading all the English and Irish slang. She created some wonderful characters, male and female, all ages. My favorite character in this book was the 2-year old Ema,</span>
  <span id="freeText5633485707713897273" style="display:none">What a welcome respite from the heaviness I’ve seemed to be reading lately. This is a not-quite-chic-lit book, and the characters, what characters they are! This is my first experience with Marian Keyes, and I have to read more. This particular novel takes place in Ireland and London (as I suppose most of her work does), and I loved reading all the English and Irish slang. She created some wonderful characters, male and female, all ages. My favorite character in this book was the 2-year old Ema, who reminds me so much of my own 3-year old, always coming through with something hilarious to bring joy back into joyless situations. Here’s an example: (To set the scene, Ema’s mother Lily is speaking - she is in the throes of writing a charming new book about the joys of life, and she tries it out on her own mother and Ema.)<br /><br /><br />That first night I read what I had written to Mum and Ema.<br />“Darling, it’s adorable,” Mum said.<br />“Dirty,” Ema agreed. “Filthy.”<br />Another passage:<br /><br />Daily, I continued to write, the words pouring from me, and every night, when we put Ema to bed, I read that day’s work and Mum raved about it. Ema, too, offered comments. (“Jiggy.” “Seedy.” “Farty.”)<br /><br />Funny stuff! I also loved the Russian neighbor Irina who works at the make-up counter. I felt like I could go on reading about these characters for much longer than the 500+ pages Keyes delivered.<br /><br />I’m not offering much in the way of plot lines here, but the book really gets into the publishing industry, which I found fascinating. It illustrates the relationships between authors (hopeful and already signed), their agents, the publishers, and the readers who love or hate them.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5633485707713897273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3567635533372643568">The heroine of this book is a fun loving Irish girl who gets stuck in the middle of many misfortunes. Due to a turn of events, she has to stop her current life and help out her family. While the story starts off where you are feeling sorry for the main character, Marian Keyes does a great job of reeling the reader into the storyline and she does a great job of keeping the reader entertained throughout the book, no matter the subject.   <span id="freeText3567635533372643568" style="display:none">The heroine of this book is a fun loving Irish girl who gets stuck in the middle of many misfortunes. Due to a turn of events, she has to stop her current life and help out her family. While the story starts off where you are feeling sorry for the main character, Marian Keyes does a great job of reeling the reader into the storyline and she does a great job of keeping the reader entertained throughout the book, no matter the subject. This book is a page turner and keeps the reader wondering what will happen to the heroine until the very end. She takes her misfortunes and she makes them positive, and in the end her life might turn out better then it was before.<br /><br />This is a fun read if you would like to do some light reading before bed, or lounging around on a Saturday afternoon. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050903637" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5283209912308810875">This book was full of potential, but the characters were AWFUL. It could have been really funny. <br/><br/>Gemma - she was bearable, but so, so bitchy. Anyone out there saying "but woman are bitchy" - you've seen nothing yet. She's so hung up on losing her man that she considers his daughter "half mine". I'm rereading this just because I'm busy and still want to read - can put this book down easily.<br/><br/>Lily: she and her partner Anton were unbearable. I don't live in the real world per se, being just 18 and li</span>
  <span id="freeText5283209912308810875" style="display:none">This book was full of potential, but the characters were AWFUL. It could have been really funny. <br /><br />Gemma - she was bearable, but so, so bitchy. Anyone out there saying "but woman are bitchy" - you've seen nothing yet. She's so hung up on losing her man that she considers his daughter "half mine". I'm rereading this just because I'm busy and still want to read - can put this book down easily.<br /><br />Lily: she and her partner Anton were unbearable. I don't live in the real world per se, being just 18 and living at home, but I know that buying Jimmy Chos and renovating with no money is so stupid. Wondering where the money is, that's even worse. That poor little girl, it'll be a miracle if they send her to school, they might decide to build a rocket using tuition fees<br /><br />JoJo: I didn't mind her, I found her story was written well. I'm not a fan of affairs but I think JoJo handled her cards well. <br /><br />Gemma's Mam: I can't stand to read pages with her. I refuse. She is an idiot. Yep, her husband left her for another women.my parents were together a long time too when they split. My mum managed to get dressed and survive without fake heart attacksAND she pays bills!! My god!! Gemma's Mam was so out there and ridiculous, of the people I've encountered - divorcees and widows - no one carried on half as bad as Gemma's Mam. <br /><br />Gemma's emails were. Rude and unfunny, don't know how Susan deals. 1/5, thanks to JoJo.</span>

<div id="review_89407175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89407175" />
    <a title="Josie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1291628-josie"><img alt="Josie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392392492p2/1291628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89407175?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josie" href="/user/show/1291628-josie">Josie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Josie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1727656-sarah">Sarah</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1291628-josie?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89407175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17999291476806050626">Firstly, I would just like to boast that I read this 600+ page book in ONE DAY. Completely, started it in the morning, finished in the evening. And so if I managed to do that, it must have caught my interest. And, well, yes it did. I was never bored, I just kept reading and reading, sucked into the stories of these three women. BUT it's the kind of book that I probably wouldn't choose to read again, nor will I remember much of it in a month's time. And now comes complaint time, because I found I</span>
  <span id="freeText17999291476806050626" style="display:none">Firstly, I would just like to boast that I read this 600+ page book in ONE DAY. Completely, started it in the morning, finished in the evening. And so if I managed to do that, it must have caught my interest. And, well, yes it did. I was never bored, I just kept reading and reading, sucked into the stories of these three women. BUT it's the kind of book that I probably wouldn't choose to read again, nor will I remember much of it in a month's time. And now comes complaint time, because I found I didn't really relate to any of the three characters, and they all did things that really annoyed and frustrated me! <br />Firstly, Lily. I've always found it slightly distressing, actually, to read or watch characters who have no idea about managing money go about wrecking their lives. I just cannot fathom why you would buy an expensive house when you did not have a fixed, steady income to pay back the loan - but worse than this is the fact that even though they were broke, they went out on a shopping spree in a ridiculously expensive store, never mind the consequences of THE BANK TAKING THE HOUSE. It just reminded me of watching <i>Middlemarch</i>, when Tertius and his STUPID wife kept on spending well beyond their means, and she just didn't get it. Yes, like I said; it makes me distressed.<br />And Gemma...well Gemma wasn't too bad, apart from her obsession about a boyfriend she had YEARS before, who was 'stolen' by her best friend, oh, and the awful way she treated Owen.<br />But most annoying was Jojo (and no, it wasn't just her name!) who, apart from doing something I completely disagree with on moral and stupidity grounds, sounded like an adolescent for most of her parts of the story. I understand the author trying to give each of the characters different voices, but is it really realistic to have a 33 year old intelligent career woman saying 'like' and 'you know' every tenth word? And things weren't 'very' tempting, oh no, they were 'way, WAY' tempting, like, you know?<br />Hmmm...but I still read it all in one day!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17999291476806050626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16888100589574703126">I do so enjoy Marian Keyes' books; they're thick and full of real people and a combination of everyday and extraordinary circumstances, and I am always at least curious about how things will come out, if not actively caring. <br/><br/>This one involved three protagonists, and the bookjacket blurb drew a few links between them, and I expected there to be a big encounter between the three of them, but they seemed never to be in the same room at the same time.   <span id="freeText16888100589574703126" style="display:none">I do so enjoy Marian Keyes' books; they're thick and full of real people and a combination of everyday and extraordinary circumstances, and I am always at least curious about how things will come out, if not actively caring. <br /><br />This one involved three protagonists, and the bookjacket blurb drew a few links between them, and I expected there to be a big encounter between the three of them, but they seemed never to be in the same room at the same time. It read like three books loosely knitted together into a single novel, with publishing being the unifying thread. Not that I didn't enjoy it, but the "only sort of" linking didn't quite work for me. It didn't feel as polished as some of her other stuff, and the varying POV's (two first-person, and one third-person) felt awkward in some ways. </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15816683993481161401">I really, really wanted to like this book more than I did.<br/><br/>I loved the idea, and some of the writing was brilliant, but it was the characters that let it down for me.<br/><br/>Gemma was kind of forgettable and a bit arrogant, although I'll admit that I took her side over the whole Lily thing. But it's a sad state of affairs when a reader is hoping that more bad stuff happens to a character, and this is what I found myself doing with Lily. I enjoyed every single bit of her suffering. There was just somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText15816683993481161401" style="display:none">I really, really wanted to like this book more than I did.<br /><br />I loved the idea, and some of the writing was brilliant, but it was the characters that let it down for me.<br /><br />Gemma was kind of forgettable and a bit arrogant, although I'll admit that I took her side over the whole Lily thing. But it's a sad state of affairs when a reader is hoping that more bad stuff happens to a character, and this is what I found myself doing with Lily. I enjoyed every single bit of her suffering. There was just something so unpleasant about her, even though she is supposed to be nice.<br /><br />And as for Jojo....I found it hard to swallow that anyone with any notions of a serious career would call themselves 'Jojo'. In addition, I just found her to be so over the top and exciting that she seemed a bit cartoonish.<br /><br />In all I enjoyed this book, but just not as much as I've enjoyed other Keyes novels.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1908549828297182328">I like Marian Keyes, that's why I bought this book. <br/><br/>I always think that every writer sort of take something from the writer's life into the book. Especially the first book. And, I sometimes think Marian Keyes does the same. Especially if you read Under The Duvet. But, so what, if Marian Keyes decided to write from something happened in her true life? This time, in The Other Side of The Story, it's her life as a writer. I guess.<br/><br/>It's a book of writer, and publisher. With it's glamorous and not so </span>
  <span id="freeText1908549828297182328" style="display:none">I like Marian Keyes, that's why I bought this book. <br /><br />I always think that every writer sort of take something from the writer's life into the book. Especially the first book. And, I sometimes think Marian Keyes does the same. Especially if you read Under The Duvet. But, so what, if Marian Keyes decided to write from something happened in her true life? This time, in The Other Side of The Story, it's her life as a writer. I guess.<br /><br />It's a book of writer, and publisher. With it's glamorous and not so glamorous life. When ideas flowing like a river through the hands of the writer, when writer's block arrived. You can get a glimpse of what's writer life look like? <br /><br />It's a book of love and betrayal. When a lover run way, when a lover lie, when a lover meet the mistress, when two lover finally end up happily after going up and down.<br /><br />Although I had stuck two time (the first third part of the book, and the last three-quarter of the book), I like the book. In fact, due to my intense moment with this book, I had a row with the bf of me *wink*.<br /><br />and, this book gave me idea on how I should write my little project.. yipeee<br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8556711658655504433">Marian Keyes is such a doll. I've met her twice.   <span id="freeText8556711658655504433" style="display:none">Marian Keyes is such a doll. I've met her twice. Once when she did an event at the store I managed and another time when she was back through town and I was lucky enough to have lunch with her. She is one of the loveliest women I have ever met. And I loved this book too! I had a lot of fun with it because it was about an author, a literary agent and an event planner (I've worked in the book biz for years and have also worked as an event planner). The book is told from the points of view of all three women who know each other and who's lives intersect but not so much that you are hearing the same story three times. Bad review, fun book.A perfect beach read!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6752294529517439253">Another Keyes, another long book. But unlike her other stories, which I can find painfully full of pointless detail, this one at least was spread amongst 3 different people, so if one was annoying, it wouldn't be too long before another one came in. But unfortunately, 2 out of 3 protags were annoying.<br/><br/>Protag #1 is a whiny, revenge-seeking crazy-person whose boyfriend moves to London (from Dublin) and then hooks up with her friend.   <span id="freeText6752294529517439253" style="display:none">Another Keyes, another long book. But unlike her other stories, which I can find painfully full of pointless detail, this one at least was spread amongst 3 different people, so if one was annoying, it wouldn't be too long before another one came in. But unfortunately, 2 out of 3 protags were annoying.<br /><br />Protag #1 is a whiny, revenge-seeking crazy-person whose boyfriend moves to London (from Dublin) and then hooks up with her friend. Please, like you weren't going to break up anyway. Her father leaves her mother and for some reason, her mother becomes and helpless slag and she has to take care of her.<br /><br />Protag #2 is the women the boyfriend left Protag #1 for and she is an insecure dreamer who writes some book and sells it to Protag #3.<br /><br />Protag #3 is a book agent. She was my favourite as she took no shit from anyone, even though she was sleeping with a co-worker. She has a melt down near the end, which is kind of annoying, but luckily, she moves past that quickly and gets back to her normal self.<br /><br />Protag #1 writes a book as well about her parents but only wants Protag #3 to rep it because she reps Protage #2 and she wants to bring her down because she stole her boyfriend. I hate shit like this automatically. Why does anyone want to be with someone who doesn't want to be with them in the first place? MOVE ON! Blah.<br /><br />Grade: C-</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481557364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15648328003952940323">Marian Keyes manages to win my heart again. <br/>After reading my first of her novels a few months ago, I thought this is an author I need to read more of. <br/>After now reading three books, I can safely say Marian is one of my favourite authors. I don't often read chick lit, but when I do I generally lean towards books set in the UK/Ireland. <br/>This one in particular peaked my interest because it was set around two authors and an publishing agent. Being someone interested in that sort of job (and studying </span>
  <span id="freeText15648328003952940323" style="display:none">Marian Keyes manages to win my heart again. <br />After reading my first of her novels a few months ago, I thought this is an author I need to read more of. <br />After now reading three books, I can safely say Marian is one of my favourite authors. I don't often read chick lit, but when I do I generally lean towards books set in the UK/Ireland. <br />This one in particular peaked my interest because it was set around two authors and an publishing agent. Being someone interested in that sort of job (and studying editing and proofreading at the moment) I generally find myself picking up those kinds of books. <br />But what really won me over, these girls are REAL. They have their flaws, they can be bitchy, feisty, deceitful... but they have good hearts. <br />The mother in Gemma's story was overbearing, annoying and was wayyy too dependant, but she was REAL. And I know that I've enjoyed a book when I am thoroughly and intensely frustrated with one of the characters, because everyone feels that way in real life about at least one person they know. <br />I love Jimmy and was so glad the ending worked out the way it did. <br />There were a lot of moments where I was completely shocked and moved by the story, Marian has yet again managed to influence me and make me feel as though I am a part of the story and these people are my friends. <br />I intend on buying every single one of her novels for my collection and look forward to reading another MK book asap. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15648328003952940323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780718146375" href="/book/show/1045987.The_Other_Side_of_the_Story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8199801-hannah?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8199801-hannah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8199801-hannah?shelf=did-not-keep">did-not-keep</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529610518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5156812671989611300">Gemma is hilarious and Jojo is fabulous, but Lily is just self-centred and boring. I don't know how but Keyes makes me desperately sorry for Jojo stuck as a mistress and of course you feel for Gemma as life seemingly crumbles. But Lily just annoyed me with her continually dithering about how horrible life is. Of course you won't have many friends when you steal one if their boyfriends (every one knows you never dip your toes in that water!). And really your life isn't do bad - beautiful child, l</span>
  <span id="freeText5156812671989611300" style="display:none">Gemma is hilarious and Jojo is fabulous, but Lily is just self-centred and boring. I don't know how but Keyes makes me desperately sorry for Jojo stuck as a mistress and of course you feel for Gemma as life seemingly crumbles. But Lily just annoyed me with her continually dithering about how horrible life is. Of course you won't have many friends when you steal one if their boyfriends (every one knows you never dip your toes in that water!). And really your life isn't do bad - beautiful child, loving partner &amp; book published! It's a veritable check list! <br /><br />But then she grew a pair (sorry for the expression - so unlike me but I was rather inspired by Jojo's hard talking American ways) and I liked her again. As did the other two just in time for me not to throw the book down in frustration. Happy endings all round! But you expect nothing less in this genre.<br /><br />My only question to the author would be this: did you realise as you were panning Lily and Gemma's books that you were also writing a bunch of unrealistic nonsense in the same genes as their's?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5156812671989611300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8283709299479251175">NOPE.. just, no ..<br/><br/><br/><br/>Fist of all, I need to mention that my rating might have due to the fact that this kind of book is not my favorite genre.   <span id="freeText8283709299479251175" style="display:none">NOPE.. just, no ..<br /><br /><br /><br />Fist of all, I need to mention that my rating might have due to the fact that this kind of book is not my favorite genre. Moreover, the rating might have been affected by the thickness of the book. It also might have been because this book was not a high priority and had lots of books which I ached for reading them. Therefor, my review might not be credible. <br /><br /><br />Lets start with what the story is about, the story involves three main characters: Gemma, she receives a phone call from her mother that her father is leaving them for his secretary. She makes a book based on it and gets and agent, Jojo, whose Lily's agent. The second character is Lily, Gemma's used-to-be friend, because ,as Gemma thinks, Lily stole Gemma's boyfriend, Anton. The next one is Jojo, their agent, she is having an affair with her Manger, Mark and these three ladies lives intertwine.<br /><br />What I feel about the characters is that they were annoying, well, Gemma is the most annoying and easily-to-hate of the three of them. First because, she spends so much time hating on her friend, and keeps dreaming that Anton might get back to her. She hooks up with a young man, Owen, and tells him that they are not in a "real relationship", <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but when he leaves her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, she cries and act as if he dumped her. In addition, she has nothing to do with her life she, somehow, stalks and wants to know everything about Lily and Anton, and keeps hoping that they will brake up , I mean, come on get a life you brat!!! <br /><br />Lily is also a need-to-slap women. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She abandons Anton after all what he have done to her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He gets her the agent, buys a house for them and does almost do everything for her. The guy is madly in love with her and she blames <i>him</i>, not them for losing the house. I just cant accept her attitude and how she doesn't see that she is as wrong as him.<br /><br />While Jojo is my least "hateable" character in this book. I mean she is strong and everything. But her fault is that she is too proud, there is this incident where she blames Mark for not letting her persuade her plan, she is an independent woman, why she listens to his opinion and then blame him?? But I feel sorry for her, although she was at some point stubborn and annoying, but I like her. <i>I shipped Jim Sweetmen with her, or the flower boy"</i><br /><br />Not to mention, Gemma's mam was ridiculous. She does talk to her neighbor just because she made a cake for her other neighbor's daughter birthday, which the later asked the former. I mean it is not her fault, what should she do?? I mean she too need to get a life , oh yea, her husband left her for a young women. My bad..<br /> <br />The plot was meh.. It was slow but , I admit, then it went decently. Again, I should mention that it might have to do with the fact that it was 600+ pages, which I only accept if it was a fantasy or destopian book. I guess it was because it is somehow three small stories in one book, I don't know.<br />At some point I felt like I preferred reading about Cody or Johnny or Jim's stories rather than these women. Moreover, at some parts it got a bit confusing who was who, lots of characters were going on and whether it was a fantasy or reality <i>maybe I was not reading the book very well</i>. Also, while writing this review, I remembered the reviews in the book, how people were being mean to Lily's book. I hope I am not mean to Marian Keyes. <i>"If you are reading this Marian, I respect you"</i><br /><br />To sum up, the book was at some point funny and cringe-y at others. The Russian lady, Cody, Manooj, Owen and jJm were cool. And as I said, it was simply not my type and I wanted to read other books which might have affected and blinded my judgment. And I must admit that I came out knowing more about publishing and writing books from <i>The Other Side of the Story</i>.<br /></span>

<div id="review_79965771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79965771" />
    <a title="Amanda Patterson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson"><img alt="Amanda Patterson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510113725p2/3010986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79965771?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Patterson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Patterson" href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson">Amanda Patterson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79965771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3885194616042936973">Marianne Keyes is back to her best with her latest offering about three whacky women in the London Publishing World. Gemma, JoJo and Lily are all involved in the world of writing. Lily as an author, by choice, Gemma, as her rival, by chance, and Jojo as a literary agent.<br/><br/>I loved the insider’s view onto this world of words and wordsmiths and the people who make their money from both of them. <br/><br/>Gemma is having a ‘lust’ affair with a younger man in Ireland, and a flirtation with a pharmacist on the si</span>
  <span id="freeText3885194616042936973" style="display:none">Marianne Keyes is back to her best with her latest offering about three whacky women in the London Publishing World. Gemma, JoJo and Lily are all involved in the world of writing. Lily as an author, by choice, Gemma, as her rival, by chance, and Jojo as a literary agent.<br /><br />I loved the insider’s view onto this world of words and wordsmiths and the people who make their money from both of them. <br /><br />Gemma is having a ‘lust’ affair with a younger man in Ireland, and a flirtation with a pharmacist on the side. She’s also still yearning for her true love, Anton, who left her for London and her best friend, Lily.<br /><br />Lily is an author who hits on a magical recipe with her flighty book, “Mimi’s Remedies” after years of struggling to have her real work published. She’s an overnight sensation and then a terrible failure. She has a baby, an unsuccessful boyfriend and a mortgage she can’t afford. <br /><br />Jojo is an American living in London (Must be a Madonna thing). She just happens to be an ex-policewoman who is one of the hottest agents at Lipman Haigh. She is engaged in a love affair with her married boss, Mark Avery. They trade witty emails and have lots of good sex, but something’s not quite right. Keyes weaves the lives of these three women together with a light touch. She is often funny, and poignant when she means to be.<br /><br />I enjoyed Rachel’s Holiday and Watermelon. I was frustrated by Last Chance Saloon and Angels. Perhaps Keyes was trying too hard. The Other Side of the Story is not meant to be deep. It is probably best described as chick-lit but I enjoyed it. It is an entertaining read that kept me giggling for a couple of nights in a row. In fact, it’s a perfect book to snuggle up with on a cold winter’s night.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3885194616042936973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339229411?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noor Ashadawi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noor Ashadawi" href="/user/show/9333266-noor-ashadawi">Noor Ashadawi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339229411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8835628467852137565">This book was very disappointing. It’s the first book I’ve read for Marian Keyes and I picked it up because of the excellent reviews it got.<br/><br/> I honestly don’t get it! It was supposed to be a story of three ladies whose lives are connected through the publishing world; a publishing agent and two authors who happen to be two ex-best friends (obviously because of a Guy… DAAHHHH). The idea is that we would normally judge these women based on the less than honorable decisions they have made but that t</span>
  <span id="freeText8835628467852137565" style="display:none">This book was very disappointing. It’s the first book I’ve read for Marian Keyes and I picked it up because of the excellent reviews it got.<br /><br /> I honestly don’t get it! It was supposed to be a story of three ladies whose lives are connected through the publishing world; a publishing agent and two authors who happen to be two ex-best friends (obviously because of a Guy… DAAHHHH). The idea is that we would normally judge these women based on the less than honorable decisions they have made but that there is always “another side of the story”. Unfortunately, the author failed at coming up with another side to the story that would make me sympathize or relate to the characters. There wasn’t even a solid link between the three characters and they didn’t even meet once. I felt that the book was very piecy, shallow and honesty.. very boring. At least with the two ex-best friends there were two different versions of the same story regardless of how unconvincing it was. Hence the title.. “The other side of the story”. But why add a twist to the publishing agent’s story that would just make me judge her without clearly giving it the proper justification so I could at least attempt to sympathize or understand the character? The story of the agent is part of the “two sides to every story” theme as you might assume but sadly, we were only given the 1 dimensional version of that story. Overall, very disappointing</span>
  <a data-text-id="8835628467852137565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/805844-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515036991p2/805844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61176003?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/805844-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amanda by: </span>
      Nicola Mcfall
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer61176003&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61176003" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15006574708613142705">I liked this book better than I had expected. I very rarely read 'chick lit', but it can be nice to relax with, something cozy and mindless (meant in the best way!). I really liked Jojo, I loved how she lived in a very grey area - she was having an affair with a married man, but she felt so guilty and couldn't bear to be the cause of a broken home. Gemma seemed really immature for her age, and her whole writing thing really bugged me. The story she wrote sounded crap and it didn't seem fair to r</span>
  <span id="freeText15006574708613142705" style="display:none">I liked this book better than I had expected. I very rarely read 'chick lit', but it can be nice to relax with, something cozy and mindless (meant in the best way!). I really liked Jojo, I loved how she lived in a very grey area - she was having an affair with a married man, but she felt so guilty and couldn't bear to be the cause of a broken home. Gemma seemed really immature for her age, and her whole writing thing really bugged me. The story she wrote sounded crap and it didn't seem fair to reward that sort of non-effort with money. Lily I sort of liked, but sort of didn't. It annoyed me how paranoid she was about Gemma getting revenge. I really really disliked Anton, I never figured out what Lily, or Gemma, saw in him. He hurt Gemma, and even though they were broken up at the time he didn't even care. Even though Lily was so upset over it, he still didn't care! And he was happy to sit back and be depressed over his crap job and let Lily stress over writing without even bothering to <i>try</i> and do anything to save them. I liked the way the story was told from every viewpoint, so that you got to fully understand what happened. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15006574708613142705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749472088?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749472088" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3390351746994340735">I've owned this book for ages and trying to get through the books I have and never read. Whilst this is a standard chic lit I'd be happy to pass on and never read again, it's actually really good! With three female characters whose lives intertwine with each other, there's enough space to love, hate and disagree with who you lie. I also love the fact that although all the characters find their own peace by the end of the book - in true chic lit style - they don't all follow the standard fairy ta</span>
  <span id="freeText3390351746994340735" style="display:none">I've owned this book for ages and trying to get through the books I have and never read. Whilst this is a standard chic lit I'd be happy to pass on and never read again, it's actually really good! With three female characters whose lives intertwine with each other, there's enough space to love, hate and disagree with who you lie. I also love the fact that although all the characters find their own peace by the end of the book - in true chic lit style - they don't all follow the standard fairy tale format. Sometimes who you love isn't right and I'm glad to see that Keyes promotes the fact that it's okay to walk away from them. I'm not happy about how some bits went - would you take a cheating spouse back? But I am willing to say that love changes, and sometimes you have to accept that and work together if you want to move on.</span>

<div id="review_3517499485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3517499485" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68189430-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598523475p2/68189430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3517499485?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/68189430-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41014305-the-other-side-of-the-story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3517499485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13978364710436274549">The only really likeable/relatable character was Jojo, mainly because she was the only one that functioned as an actual adult while still having problems and life issues to deal with - as every adult does. The other two main characters, Gemma and Lily were equally problematic both as believable functioning adults and as likeable characters - it got old quick and by about half way I was just hanging out to see how things turned out for Jojo. But ultimately any promises set up in the first half of</span>
  <span id="freeText13978364710436274549" style="display:none">The only really likeable/relatable character was Jojo, mainly because she was the only one that functioned as an actual adult while still having problems and life issues to deal with - as every adult does. The other two main characters, Gemma and Lily were equally problematic both as believable functioning adults and as likeable characters - it got old quick and by about half way I was just hanging out to see how things turned out for Jojo. But ultimately any promises set up in the first half of the novel were not delivered in the second half.<br /><br />****SPOILERS PAST THIS POINT****<br /><br /><br />I also found the ending extremely unfulfilling. Jojo was the only character I was rooting for and the fact that she was having an affair did not take away from her or Mark's humanity in the situation. Not only that - but marriages do fall apart, it's fact. Separations can occur civically and in which the family can still function happily and healthily with divorced parents. Given the setup work done in the previous 450 pages it was clear that both Jojo, Mark, and the wife involved probably could have managed a fairly drama free separation. But the kids kept coming up as an excuse not to go ahead with Mark leaving a sexless and unfulfilling marriage. The climax in their storyline is frustrating and dissapointing. I was so angry after reading nearly 500 pages of this book, hanging out for the one character I liked to get their act together and it never happens.<br /><br />I felt Marian probably needed to add some more flaws to Jojo and Mark's relationship, or make the kids/wife a bigger issue somehow because there just did not seem to be enough reasons there for Jojo and Mark not to go through with the separation - it really seemed like something they could figure out. I regret reading this book for that reason, and every time I look at it I still feel that sense of disappointment. It could have been a good book despite that if Gemma and Lilly were edited to be a bit more realistic in their functionality. Overall I was more frustrated by the character's choices, did not feel overly satisfied with the ending. Which is annoying because I think Keyes can write. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13978364710436274549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10643549-judy?shelf=english-setting">english-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10643549-judy?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer10678572300212747468">This book shares the story of three loosely related women in Ireland and England. The first time it switched points of view, I literally thought the kindle book had suddenly switched to another book altogether. After that though, I enjoyed it, although I can't say that any of the three women was a completely sympathetic character. I felt desperately sorry for Gemma (an event planner who would like to be an author), whose mother latched onto her when her father left her for another woman, and wou</span>
  <span id="freeText10678572300212747468" style="display:none">This book shares the story of three loosely related women in Ireland and England. The first time it switched points of view, I literally thought the kindle book had suddenly switched to another book altogether. After that though, I enjoyed it, although I can't say that any of the three women was a completely sympathetic character. I felt desperately sorry for Gemma (an event planner who would like to be an author), whose mother latched onto her when her father left her for another woman, and wouldn't even let Gemma spend the night in her own apartment for almost a year. And yet, Gemma spends her spare time plotting against a former friend, Lily (an author), who ended up with Gemma's "boyfriend", although it's not clear to me that they were really still involved when it happened. Lily and Anton, the couple in question, seem incapable of acting like grownups in regard to money. And then there's Jojo, a literary agent who is having an affair with her married boss and trying desperately to make partner when the next partner retires. Jojo ends up representing both Lily and Gemma eventually. Despite those quibbles, I was interested enough to finish it pretty quickly, so I guess it couldn't have been that bad!</span>

<div id="review_2033722027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033722027" />
    <a title="Dark-Draco" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18484922-dark-draco"><img alt="Dark-Draco" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363942329p2/18484922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033722027?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark-Draco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark-Draco" href="/user/show/18484922-dark-draco">Dark-Draco</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140295993" href="/book/show/924487.The_Other_Side_of_the_Story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18484922-dark-draco?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2033722027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer619034504127355119">Fantastic and Fun!<br/><br/>This has never been my favourite genre, but Keyes writes a damn good story! What usually puts me off of 'chic-lit' is how man obsessed the characters are - as if finding true love is the only thing of any importance in their world. But not so here. <br/><br/>This is the story of three women. Lily is living with Anton. Gemma used to be with Anton. Jojo is a literary agent representing them both. Gemma's Dad has walked out on his Mum. Jojo is sleeping with her boss. Lily has writer's block</span>
  <span id="freeText619034504127355119" style="display:none">Fantastic and Fun!<br /><br />This has never been my favourite genre, but Keyes writes a damn good story! What usually puts me off of 'chic-lit' is how man obsessed the characters are - as if finding true love is the only thing of any importance in their world. But not so here. <br /><br />This is the story of three women. Lily is living with Anton. Gemma used to be with Anton. Jojo is a literary agent representing them both. Gemma's Dad has walked out on his Mum. Jojo is sleeping with her boss. Lily has writer's block. And essentially that is it! But it is written in such an entertaining way, with plenty of laughs and OMG moments. And while Man troubles do beset the characters, it definitely isn't the 'be-all-and-end-all' of their lives.<br /><br />I have to admit to not liking Gemma to start with, and really not liking her Mum, who seemed too dippy for words, but she did grow on me towards the end. I kind of liked her attitude. I loved Jojo - who wouldn't want to be described as Jessica Rabbit?!?! - and really liked how her story progressed. Lily - hmmm - a hard one as, to be honest, her story seemed the least focused, but again, I liked her ending.<br /><br />So overall, highly recommended reading - a chance to enjoy something light and entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="619034504127355119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2741586039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741586039" />
    <a title="Laurie Hoppe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59313251-laurie-hoppe"><img alt="Laurie Hoppe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473042473p2/59313251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741586039?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie Hoppe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie Hoppe" href="/user/show/59313251-laurie-hoppe">Laurie Hoppe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140295993" href="/book/show/924487.The_Other_Side_of_the_Story">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59313251-laurie-hoppe?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741586039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1434406769463186633">First off, this is the first Marian Keyes that I've read in a long time, and I love her style. She's warm and witty and there are moments of such complete identification I either smiled or hurt when I read them. The Dublin/London setting charms me, too. (This is the only novel I've ever read with characters named Aoife and Manoj.)<br/><br/>It's about three 30-something women: Gemma, Lily and JoJo. Brunette Gemma is an event planner whose life is upended when her father leaves her mother for another woman,</span>
  <span id="freeText1434406769463186633" style="display:none">First off, this is the first Marian Keyes that I've read in a long time, and I love her style. She's warm and witty and there are moments of such complete identification I either smiled or hurt when I read them. The Dublin/London setting charms me, too. (This is the only novel I've ever read with characters named Aoife and Manoj.)<br /><br />It's about three 30-something women: Gemma, Lily and JoJo. Brunette Gemma is an event planner whose life is upended when her father leaves her mother for another woman, and Mam is almost incapacitated by the shock and grief. Lily is a shy, blonde wanna be author whose career unexpectedly takes off after she's mugged. Redhaired JoJo is a high-powered London literary agent, a NY transplant who happened onto publishing and is determined to make a success of herself. I won't give away how their lives intersect, but they do. Yes, they have men, but this story centers on the women.<br /><br />So why not 5 stars? The ending seems rushed. After 500 pages of a certain pace, the acceleration of events kinda rattled me. And then there's Lily. I'm clearly supposed to like her, she may even be meant to be my favorite. But she's too wishy-washy, too idiosyncratic. I admit that whenever I saw a Lily chapter begin, I toyed with skipping it. I didn't, which is good because they always moved the plot along. But she did bug me. (Now her baby, Ema! There's a charmer! Her favorite toy isn't a doll or a plush bear, it's a wrench named "Jessie.")</span>
  <a data-text-id="1434406769463186633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_407031156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407031156" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6182286-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407031156?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/6182286-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407031156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12067456994940129931">I’m currently re-reading The Other Side of the Story. Previously I had rated it four stars, but I had to change it to three stars. I don’t know how I missed this before - but the characters are really frustrating. I often say that there doesn’t have to be a “hero/ine” and not all the characters have to be likeable (in fact, I quite like controversial characters), but these characters are just annoying. Gemma is mean, Lily comes across as weak, and Jojo is a cheat (although she’s still my favouri</span>
  <span id="freeText12067456994940129931" style="display:none">I’m currently re-reading The Other Side of the Story. Previously I had rated it four stars, but I had to change it to three stars. I don’t know how I missed this before - but the characters are really frustrating. I often say that there doesn’t have to be a “hero/ine” and not all the characters have to be likeable (in fact, I quite like controversial characters), but these characters are just annoying. Gemma is mean, Lily comes across as weak, and Jojo is a cheat (although she’s still my favourite out of the three). #RantOver. I’m not saying don’t read the book - I love Marian Keyes, but reading her older stuff now, I have a new appreciation for her more recent novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12067456994940129931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_6063187'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6063187-twenties-girl"><img alt="Twenties Girl" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1320544759l/6063187._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tPRdiQcQIQx1Iq3u9taIX9+NpMf79Q8UVfze3rx5V+n1V3O7xcV0W4HjdNlRhucJAsa8f88KAwFfuzPanYDhqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<span id="freeTextContainer13688120217516202981">Marian Keyes (born 10 September 1963) is an Irish novelist and non-fiction writer, best known for her work in women's literature. She is an Irish Book Awards winner. Over 22 million copies of her novels have been sold worldwide and her books have been translated into 32 languages. She became known worldwide for <i>Watermelon</i>, <i>Lucy Sullivan is Getting Married</i>, and <i>This Charming Man</i>, with themes includ</span>
  <span id="freeText13688120217516202981" style="display:none">Marian Keyes (born 10 September 1963) is an Irish novelist and non-fiction writer, best known for her work in women's literature. She is an Irish Book Awards winner. Over 22 million copies of her novels have been sold worldwide and her books have been translated into 32 languages. She became known worldwide for <i>Watermelon</i>, <i>Lucy Sullivan is Getting Married</i>, and <i>This Charming Man</i>, with themes including domestic violence and alcoholism.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13688120217516202981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
